Message: 		<html><head><title>There is a new comment to Corporate cell plan!!!</title></head><body><p>There is a new comment to Corporate cell plan!!!.</p>
<p>Comment Link: https://staff.powertochange.org/information-technology/corporate-cell-plan/#comment-1523</p>
<p>Author: Keith Richmond</p>
<p>Comment: Ben, your first scenario is the correct one.  Your rate is $35-$39 per month across the 3 year term, but you get the $600 applied as a bill credit, so the net effect is no charge for plan for the first 15 months or so, then $35-$39 thereafter. The credit would be applied in $120 increments across the first five months of the three year term. Keep in mind that you would bring your own phone in this scenario. No device is supplied as part of this plan.</p>
<p>Permalink: https://staff.powertochange.org/information-technology/corporate-cell-plan/</p>

<p>Author: Keith Richmond</p>
<p>Comment: A few people on the survey asked about what happens if they recently signed up with the Rogers corporate plan, but we switch to another carrier.  In that case, there will likely be early cancellation fees from Rogers. However, other carriers will be offering activation credits when you sign up.  Our intent is to ensure those credits are equal to or greater than the cost of your early cancellation fee.</p>

<p>Author: Keith Richmond</p>
<p>Comment: Some people have asked whether they can use their recently purchase Rogers phone with the "bring your own device" scenario described in the survey if the offer is from another carrier (Bell or Telus).  The answer is yes, you can, but you will first need to get your device unlocked by Rogers.  The standard fee for unlocking is $50, and you have to have had your device on the Rogers network for at least 90 days.</p>

Message: 		<html><head><title>There is a new comment to Corporate cell plan!!!</title></head><body><p>There is a new comment to Corporate cell plan!!!.</p>
<p>Comment Link: https://staff.powertochange.org/information-technology/corporate-cell-plan/#comment-1529</p>
<p>Author: Keith Richmond</p>
<p>Comment: Lydia, pooled data is shared across staff, and that is part of our current Rogers contract.</p>
<p>Roughly, here is how it works: not everyone uses their full allotment of data and the remainder gets put in the "pool" for that month. There are some months when some people go over their allotment, but as long as there is data in the "pool", that use the excess there so no overage is charged.  </p>
<p>If the entire pool is used up, then those users exceeding their allotment will be charged an overage fee.  However, no users who are within their allotment will be charged.</p>
<p>Permalink: https://staff.powertochange.org/information-technology/corporate-cell-plan/</p>
<p>Manage your subscriptions: https://staff.powertochange.org/manage-subscriptions?srek=80c92f422183e7ac559ec077f5310bc5&srk=a2e65f67aa1e624b64ed00340c8b3621</p>

<p>Author: Keith Richmond</p>
<p>Comment: Hi Susan,</p>
<p>The new plan will certainly have a phone deal as an option.  The hypothetical offer in the survey would not be the only option. Most plans are priced to include the cost of the phone over the term. My intent in including it would be more to see who would be open to a lower cost plan where the staff member would supply the device and only pay for the plan.  There will also be standard plan with more standard rates that would include a new phone up front. </p>
<p>Regarding your old phone, it is treated like any other purchase that is made through a P2C account.  It remains P2C property and would need to be either repurposed within P2C or bought out at market price by the staff member (with director permission). If you choose the pater option, you would need to get it unlocked by Rogers if you were intending it to be used on a different carrier. I believe the charge there is $50. </p>
<p>To your last paragraph - your phone number will remain with you, even if we transition to a new carrier.  I am not quite sure what you mean by your last question, so I will contact you directly for more info. </p>
<p>Hope that helps.</p>

<p>Author: Keith Richmond</p>
<p>Comment: @IleaneP - a director may, at her or his discretion, provide a staff member with a phone on the corporate plan, and pay for it out of the department budget.  Speak to your director to discuss your situation. </p>
<p>@SusanDS - the data will still be pooled.  TELUS calls it "shared data", and that is how it is recorded in the previous post. Also, the fate of current phones is still a matter being discussed internally.  I will to to get you some clarity on that in the next week or so. </p>
<p>@BenM - Pacific CoastCom will be setting up an online staff "catalogue" that will allow staff to pursue phone options and pricing.  I don't have a date for when this will be live, but my best guess is we will have someone within two weeks.  Also, the pool combines the 3GB and 5GB data options.  This is a change from the previous Rogers arrangement where the two data options were pooled separately.</p>

<p>Comment: @KimK - any phone is fine as long as it is either unlocked or locked to Telus. If you can find a bargain, you are golden!  However, bear in mind that the prices shown in the link you provided are the subsidized prices. If you click on the phone you are interested in, it will show you the "no term" price, which is the price you would pay.  For example, that link shows the IPhone SE at $100, but if you click on the link, the "no term" price is $590 - the price you would pay.</p>

<p>Comment Link: https://staff.powertochange.org/information-technology/telus-cellular-plan-additional-information/#comment-1595</p>
<p>Author: Keith Richmond</p>
<p>Comment: @David - you are correct, on the $42 plan wit the $600 credit, the end result is about a year's worth of free service, and then $42 (plus any overages and sales tax) per month thereafter.  Alo, you essentially have described the pool correctly, except you cannot target one phone's excess specifically to anohter phone. All excess goes into a centralized pool on the account with all other staff, and then all overages get to dip into that pool to offset the overage.  If we collective exceed the data in the pool. those in excess will then be charged an overage proportional to their share of the overage.</p>

<p>Comment: Hi Josh,</p>
<p>Your understanding of "no term" pricing is correct in that it is a category for buying the phone outright or bringing your own device. There is an option to go month-to-month with the corporate plan, however, in doing so you will forgo the 600$ activation credit that comes with the BYOD plan.</p>
<p>Our relationship with Rogers will be ending, and so unfortunately you will not be able to remain on the Rogers plan indefinitely. The 600$ activation credit that TELUS provides with their BYOD plan is meant to offset the cancellation fees from Rogers.</p>

<p>Comment Link: https://staff.powertochange.org/information-technology/corporate-wireless-plan-accepting-signups/#comment-1658</p>
<p>Author: Keith Richmond</p>
<p>Comment: @HayleyS - the only way to pay for a phone is with a P2C account.  Staff paying on there own with a credit card, for example, is not an option.  I fyou need a phone for your role, please talk to your supervisor for approval, then ask them what department account is to be charged. </p>
<p>@SteveK - although you can buy unlock codes at cheaper rate online, there is no guarantee that these codes will work. Often times the process is finicky and may not work if not followed correctly. We recommend getting the unlock done through your current cellular vendor.  A bit more costly, but at least you know it will work.</p>
<p>Permalink: https://staff.powertochange.org/information-technology/corporate-wireless-plan-accepting-signups/</p>

<p>Author: Keith Richmond</p>
<p>Comment: @HayleyS - the only way to pay for a phone is with a P2C account.  Staff paying on there own with a credit card, for example, is not an option.  I fyou need a phone for your role, please talk to your supervisor for approval, then ask them what department account is to be charged. </p>
<p>@SteveK - although you can buy unlock codes at cheaper rate online, there is no guarantee that these codes will work. Often times the process is finicky and may not work if not followed correctly. We recommend getting the unlock done through your current cellular vendor.  A bit more costly, but at least you know it will work.</p>
<p>Permalink: https://staff.powertochange.org/information-technology/corporate-wireless-plan-accepting-signups/</p>
